Elementary School Party Ideology Speech Competition to Hold Preliminary Rounds for Three Days Starting Today

Time: 1:00 PM every afternoon

Location: Municipal Party Headquarters Auditorium

The Shanghai Municipal Elementary School Party Ideology Speech Competition organized by the Municipal Training Department is approaching. In order to facilitate the competition technically, enrich the content of the competition, and ensure the accuracy of the competition results, the Municipal Training Department has decided to hold preliminary rounds at the Municipal Party Headquarters for three days starting today (every day from 1:00 PM). The list of participating groups for the preliminary rounds has also been drawn by each school or entrusted to the Municipal Training Department for arrangement. The arrangement has been completed and announced in various newspapers today. The details are as follows:

List of participants for the first group preliminary round: Shangwen (Jiang Derong), Ji Xiao (Li Yue), Pudong (Lin Yongquan), Xiqu (Lu Changhua), Guangdong (Wu Zhenfen), Meixi (Zhou Zengye), Zhongdao (Wei Yuee), Suzhou Luh (Xu Meichi), Nongtan (Tang Jianhong), Yangcun (Yang Bingwei), Jiancheng (Xu Zhenyu), Shuji (Wu Wenpu), Jingye (Cai Chunsheng), Bide (Cheng Baozhu), Tangwan (Song Xueliang), Hean (Wang Xiaohu), Danhua (Ma Jinyun), Minglun (Zhou Guangfu), Shihua (Miao Dafang), Yunxue (Shen Zhengde). The above list is for today's preliminary round participants, who must arrive at 1:00 PM to draw lots to determine the order of speeches.

List of judges for the first group: Wu Xianren (Chief Executive of the Party Member Training Section of the Municipal Training Department), Zhou Yingcai (Director of Training at Qingxin Middle School), Zhou Shang (Second Section of the Municipal Education Bureau), Li Zheng (Chief Executive of the Editorial Section of the Municipal Propaganda Department). Chief Judge for the preliminary round: Jiang Huansu (Secretary of the Municipal Training Department).

Prizes and Souvenirs: The purpose of this competition is to encourage the study of Party Ideology and train speakers' abilities, which is slightly different from ordinary speech competitions. Therefore, all participants will receive souvenirs. The prizes for the finalists will be especially unique.

Judging Method: This speech competition focuses on skills and scoring is based on four aspects with varying weights: (1) Thought accounts for 30%, (2) Structure accounts for 30%, (3) Tone accounts for 20%, (4) Attitude accounts for 20%. The number of finalists selected from the preliminary round is limited to one-quarter of the participants, and the number of finalists selected from the final round is limited to one-third of the participants.

Municipal Education Bureau Completes Survey of Registered Private Elementary Schools

In order to understand the academic performance of children in all registered private elementary schools in the city and to compare the performance of municipal schools and private schools, the Municipal Education Bureau, under the direction of the Third Section, dispatched Ding Chongxuan, He Yuanzhi, Xu Dianjun, Wang Jiehe, Cao Zhen, Huang Zha, and others to conduct surveys of various private elementary schools for four items: arithmetic knowledge, common sense, dictation of characters, and silent reading, starting from October 20th. The survey was completed on the 6th of this month. A total of 40 schools, 192 classes, and 8,040 people were tested. The papers are now being graded and the scores are being calculated separately for comparison with municipal schools to determine the advantages and disadvantages.

Local News

Shanghai-Hankou Airline Plane Crashes Yesterday Morning, Commander Xiong Shihui Severely Injured

Shanghai Second Plane Plunges After Takeoff, Striking Mast

Pilot, Two Passengers Die of Injuries After Rescue Attempts

Yang Yongtai Injured in the Waist, Life Expected to Be Saved

Xiong Shihui, Songhu Garrison Commander, was summoned by Chairman Chiang to go to Jiangxi and then to Hunan, Hubei, and other provinces to inspect and assist in suppressing the communist bandits. Yesterday morning at eight o'clock, Xiong, along with General Headquarters advisor Yang Yongtai and bodyguard Zeng Chunfan, boarded China Aviation Corporation's Shanghai Second plane to go to Xunyang. They departed from Longhua Airport. The pilot was American pilot Bell, and the mechanical assistant was Bian Fugen. Passengers included Xiong and the other two men, as well as Russian woman Mrs. An Qulifu, and Yin Wenlong, manager of the Hankou Anli Foreign Firm's automobile department. The plane carried a total of seven people, but shortly after taking off, about fifty feet off the ground, the plane's right wing collided with the large mast of a sand barge. The wing broke, the mast broke, and the plane suddenly plunged to the beach on the riverbank at exactly eight minutes past eight. As a result, American pilot Bell, Chinese mechanical assistant Bian Fugen, the Russian woman, and Yin Wenlong died of severe injuries. Xiong Shihui, Yang Yongtai, and Zeng Chunfan were seriously injured. This is a unprecedented tragedy in the history of Chinese aviation. The details of the accident are described as follows:

Send-off Spectacle: Yesterday morning at 7:50, Xiong Shihui, accompanied by Yang Yongtai and others, arrived at Longhua Airport by car. Chiefs and secretaries of various departments of the Garrison Headquarters went to see them off. The area around the airport was heavily guarded by troops from the Fifth Division. The Headquarters military band was also present. Xiong and others slowly boarded the plane amidst the lively music, smiling and shaking hands with those who came to see them off.

Course of the Accident: Yesterday morning at eight o'clock, Shanghai Second plane took off from the ground. The southwest wind was strong, so the plane rose along the riverbank to the opposite bank of the Lan Nidu in Pudong, near the Rihui Bridge on the riverbank. The plane was already fifty feet off the ground when it suddenly collided with the large mast of a sand barge of about 2,000 tons moored there. With a loud crash, the right wing of the plane broke immediately, and the large mast, as wide as a hug, also broke at the same time. The plane lost its balance, and the front of the plane immediately tilted, falling from the air onto the mudflat outside Rihui Bridge, only about ten minutes after takeoff.

Rushing to the Rescue: When the plane crashed, the people seeing them off and the airline staff had not yet dispersed. Seeing this, they rushed along the riverbank to rescue. The distance from Rihui Bridge to the airport was about a mile, but the water was deep and muddy, and their clothes were soaked. Half of the plane was submerged in the mudflat. Passengers and the pilot were moaning inside, bloodstains were everywhere, and the scene was too horrible to bear. They quickly opened the plane door, called for several sampans, and carried the injured out one by one, transporting them to the airport by boat.

Pilot Dies: American pilot Bell and mechanical assistant Bian Fugen were seated in the front of the plane, so their injuries were the most severe. Bian Fugen had a large hole in his forehead, and blood flowed non-stop. Russian woman An Qulifu also suffered severe brain trauma, and her hands and feet were broken. The three were carried ashore, but were already unable to speak. Mechanical assistant Bian Fugen (above), American pilot Bell (below)

They were rushed to the Red Cross General Hospital on Haige Road for treatment. When they arrived at the hospital, Bell was already beyond medical help and died immediately. After thirty minutes, Bian Fugen and the Russian woman also died one after another. Yin Wenlong, manager of the Hankou Anli Foreign Firm's automobile department, had fractures in his right hand and right foot, and his chest and waist were also severely injured. He was rushed to Renji Hospital for emergency surgery. At twelve o'clock, at the insistence of Yin's family and friends, he was transferred to the Public Concession Hospital for X-ray examination. Due to excessive bleeding and severe brain trauma, he died at four o'clock yesterday afternoon. The body was then moved to the International Funeral Parlor. The bodies of the American pilot and Bian Fugen were moved to the Forensic Examination Office in Feilun, scheduled for court examination this morning.

Xiong's Treatment: Xiong Shihui's seat in the plane was number one, in the first row, so his injuries were less severe than those of the pilot. Situation of Shanghai Second plane after the crash (Photo by this newspaper)

After the accident, headquarters staff took him to the Longhua Headquarters by car and called the director of Baolong Hospital and a German doctor to give him emergency treatment. At the same time, they telegraphed Niu Huisheng, director of the Shanghai Private Orthopedic Hospital, to come to treat him. Niu had gone to Wusong for a morning consultation at six o'clock and did not return home until nine o'clock, then rushed to Longhua to treat him. At 9:30, Xiong and his bodyguard Zeng Sand barge broken mast and plane fallen into the river (Photo by this newspaper)

Page 14

Chunfan were taken to the Private Shanghai Orthopedic Hospital at 852 Xujiahui Road. Xiong was taken to room number one. Immediately after arriving at the hospital, Dr. Niu Huisheng performed emergency surgery, bandaging the broken left hand and right foot and injecting a cardiac stimulant. Xiong was quite lucid at the time. He fell asleep at about 11:00. X-rays were taken at 12:00 and a bone-setting operation was performed at 2:30 in the afternoon. The situation in the afternoon was better than in the morning.

Injury Report: Dr. Niu Huisheng released a report on the injuries of Xiong Shihui and Zeng Chunfan at 5:00 yesterday afternoon. The report was signed by Dr. Niu Huisheng and Niu Huilin. It is transcribed as follows: Commander Xiong Shihui has six injuries: (1) The upper segment of the left humerus is broken into three pieces. (2) The femur and tibia of the right leg are fractured. (3) Head injury with significant bleeding. (4) Right hand abrasion. (5) Rib pain in the chest. (6) Brain concussion, but still conscious. Xiong's temperature was 99.4 degrees yesterday afternoon, pulse 118, respiration 25. Aide Zeng Chunfan has four injuries: (1) Fracture of the left humerus. (2) Fracture of the right femur. (3) Rib pain. (4) Lacerations of the mouth and nose with bleeding. His temperature was 98 degrees, pulse 128, respiration 32. According to Dr. Niu, if Xiong's condition does not change within 48 hours, he should gradually recover his health, but he will need to stay in the hospital for at least two months.

Condolences Pour In: Yesterday, after hearing the news, people from all walks of life went to the orthopedic hospital to offer condolences. When Xiong was injured and taken to the Headquarters, Mayor Zhang and Public Security Bureau Chief Yuan Liang rushed to offer condolences and accompanied him to the orthopedic hospital. Shortly after, Madam Chiang Song Meiling, wife of Chiang Kai-shek, Madam Sun Ke, Chen Shaokuan, Chen Xunyong, Yang Hu, Chen Shiguang, Liu Yunfang, and others arrived one after another. They were all received by Jiang Yi, the deputy chief of staff of the Headquarters. China Aviation Corporation also sent Wang Xichang to inquire about the injuries.

Yang's Condition: Yang Yongtai's injuries were the lightest. His family took him to Baolong Hospital on Baker Road for treatment. After examination by Dr. Ruan Shangcheng, he formally announced to reporters yesterday that Yang was only injured in the waist and could not lie flat. He coughed up a mouthful of blood after arriving at the hospital, indicating that his lungs were traumatized. Currently, because he cannot stand up, X-rays cannot be taken. It is expected that the injuries will not be life-threatening. Former Shanghai Mayor Huang Fu went to Baolong Hospital to offer condolences.

Brief Biographies of the Deceased: American pilot Bell was 36 years old. He served in the aviation field during the European War and then worked as a pilot for the American Commercial Aviation Company. He came to Shanghai on October 20 to accept a position with China Aviation Corporation. Mechanical assistant Bian Fugen was a native of Wuxi, 25 years old. His father and wife were in Wuxi. He had a younger brother, Rengen, studying printing in Shanghai. Bian had been working for the airline for almost a year. He was usually diligent and hardworking and was highly valued by the authorities. He started as a trainee and was recently promoted to his current position. Yesterday, his younger brother had already telegraphed Wuxi to ask his parents to come to Shanghai to handle the funeral arrangements. Yin Wenlong was 27 years old, a native of Suzhou. He was the Chinese manager of the automobile department of the Anli Foreign Firm in Hankou. His family lived in Hankou. He came to Shanghai to negotiate business and stayed for less than a week. His sudden death is truly tragic. The Russian woman, Mrs. Zhi Qulifu, ran a tailor shop in Hankou and usually traveled between Shanghai and Hankou by plane. Yesterday morning, her friends came to the airport to see her off. Unexpectedly, she met with such a tragic fate.

Company's Aftermath: After the accident, the company sent two doctors, an American doctor and Chinese doctor Chen Jiyao, to various hospitals to treat the injured personnel. According to Nie Kaiyi, who spoke to our newspaper reporter yesterday, he was also present at the scene of the accident and witnessed that it was a great misfortune for both the company and the passengers. In addition to reporting the actual situation to the Ministry of Communications, the company is also handling the aftermath. The Shanghai-Hankou air route will continue to operate as usual. All pilots have been ordered to drive with utmost caution.

Plane Continues: Yesterday morning at 8:00, China Aviation Corporation originally planned to have two planes depart. One was the Shanghai Second plane that crashed, bound for Jiujiang and Hankou. The other was the Chongqing plane, test-flying to Yichang. The Shanghai plane was originally scheduled to have assistant pilot Chen Huazhen assist in the driving, but Bian Fugen was suddenly replaced. After the accident, the Chongqing plane was temporarily delayed. After the rescue was completed, company staff took out the mail from Shanghai Second plane and transferred it to the Chongqing plane for transport to various ports. The Chongqing plane, driven by American Hanton, departed at 10:20 yesterday morning for Nanjing, Jiujiang, Hankou, and other places.

Worth 100,000: The Shanghai Second plane was purchased when Sino-American Aviation Corporation was established. It can accommodate six passengers and two pilots and is an amphibious plane. Each plane is worth about 100,000 national currency. This time, the right wing was broken and the internal machinery was completely damaged and beyond repair. Yesterday afternoon, the wrecked plane was still in the mudflat on the riverbank. It was heard that it could not be towed ashore until today. Furthermore, according to company staff who witnessed the scene, it was fortunate that the accident occurred on a mudflat with soft soil. If it had fallen on land, none of the crew and passengers would have survived.

Lack of Technical Expertise: According to another source, American pilot Bell arrived in Shanghai on October 20 and has only been in China for a little over a month. He is not familiar with the local situation and has only driven a few times. The most skilled Chinese pilot in the airline is Lin Anjun. Last Thursday, after Lin and Bell flew the same plane back to Shanghai, Lin formally reported to the director of the airline department, American Smis, that Bell's skills were somewhat lacking and asked that he not be given the responsibility of flying. However, Smis ignored him and allowed him to fly as usual, which led to the disaster.

News This Morning: At 9:00 last night, Dr. Niu Huisheng returned to the orthopedic hospital to examine Xiong. At that time, his temperature was slightly lower, at 96 degrees. There was no change in pulse or respiration. His condition was quite good. At about 1:00 this morning, Dr. Niu went to examine Xiong again. Xiong's temperature had increased to 100.4 degrees. He was in better spirits and could drink some orange juice. Xiong's bodyguard, Zeng Chunfan, had shortness of breath in the evening, but it subsided again later in the evening. Furthermore, according to those who personally sent Xiong to board the plane yesterday, Xiong's seat in the plane was number one. His back was directly facing the back of the crew, but separated by a thick glass. Next to Xiong was Yang Yongtai. Opposite Xiong was his bodyguard Zeng Chunfan. Behind Zeng's seat was the Russian woman. Sitting with the Russian woman was Yin Wenlong. The front and rear parts of the plane were the most severely injured, while the middle part was less injured. Xiong, Yang, and Zeng happened to be in the middle part. It was also said that Yin's female relatives were also at the scene to see him off. Seeing the plane crash, they disregarded everything and waded into the water to rescue him. The situation was extremely tragic. The efforts of the Garrison Headquarters Detective Team to bravely protect and rescue Xiong were also commendable.

Mayor Zhang Hopes for Sino-British Cooperation

Speech at Yesterday's Banquet for the British Economic Mission

Mayor Zhang hosted a banquet for the entire British Economic Mission at Chen's residence at 6 Seymour Road at 7:00 last night. Those in attendance included local business leaders Wang Xiaolai, Yu Qiaqing, Liu Hongsheng, Xu Xinliu, the British Consul-General, the Commercial Counselor, Zhao Jinqing, Chen Shiguang, Wu Tiecheng, the Municipal Government Secretary-General, and the heads of various bureaus. That evening, Mayor Zhang gave a very long speech, full of sincerity. It is transcribed as follows:

Gentlemen of the British Commercial Delegation, you have come to China on a tour for the purpose of developing trade between our two countries and promoting friendship between our two nations. I would like to take this opportunity to offer you a humble feast and sincerely welcome you to do my part as a host. It is an honor to have you here. I recall that three weeks ago, my colleagues in the Municipal Government hosted a banquet to welcome the British Canadian Commercial Delegation. I was unable to attend in person due to official business in Beijing. I am even more pleased to be able to personally welcome you this time. Since the European War, the world economic situation has undergone drastic changes. Whether a country is small and densely populated or large and rich in resources, they have all been opening up new markets abroad to exchange what they have for what they lack, so that the problems of overproduction and unemployment can be solved to some extent. This time, the United Kingdom has specially sent Sir Ernest Thompson to lead the British Far East Economic Mission to tour East Asia. Its purpose is to investigate the current state of trade in the Far East, the future development trends, and the perceptions of the Chinese government and people towards the United Kingdom, and then plan how to cooperate with China for mutual benefit to develop future trade and how to compare with other countries to restore its inherent trading position. Its impact on political, economic, industrial, and commercial circles between China and Britain is extremely important and significant. As a host, we should sincerely express our welcome and, for the sake of the future development of Sino-British trade, we should discuss with sincerity and vision, so that in addition to the reception and banquet, we will have infinite expectations. Now, I would like to briefly express my views on Sino-British trade relations. According to this year's customs records, the trade situation between the United Kingdom and its British territories, excluding Hong Kong, still maintains its inherent position. For example, in 1929, imports accounted for 21.67% of China's total imports, while in 1928, they only accounted for 19.6%. Both imports and exports show an increasing trend. For example, in 1922, the value of goods transported from China to Britain was only 38,507,874 taels of customs silver. In 1929, it jumped to 74,334,237 taels. In 1929, the value of goods transported from Britain to China was 119,148,969 taels. Although it was slightly lower than in 1922, 1923 and 1924, it was 44,076,575 taels higher than in 1927. The speed of its progress can be seen generally. Currently, the goods transported from Britain to China are mainly steel, textiles, machinery, piece goods, and tinplate. This is because cities in China have been actively innovating and striving for construction in recent years. Most of the houses built are made of steel bars and concrete, so the sales of building steel and plain iron bars are extremely wide. These goods are mostly ordered from British and Belgian companies. Furthermore, the import of steel wire rope is mostly used for mines, especially salt mines in Sichuan, which are also supplied in large quantities by British and American manufacturers. As for British tinplate, it will continue to be imported to supply canned food manufacturers. This industry is becoming increasingly developed in China, so the future sales of tinplate can be predicted. In addition, high-quality artificial silk operated by British merchants will still maintain its original status. In recent years, the production of artificial silk has been abundant, the price is low, and the quality is good. Its promotion in China may not always be smooth. This is the general situation of goods transported from Britain to China. Now, let us discuss the goods exported from China to Britain, which should be mainly soybeans, soybean products, eggs, egg products, and other agricultural products. For example, in recent years, the soybean market in Manchuria has been improving, and the harvest is quite abundant. Every season, more and more goods are transported to Japan and Europe. Furthermore, the sales of soybean oil exported to various parts of Europe have also improved significantly. In the past, households in the country used soybean oil as fuel, but now they have switched to foreign oil, so soybean oil is mostly sold abroad, and exports are booming. This is also a major reason. As for eggs and egg products, they are also a major export from China. For example, every winter, the climate in Europe is extremely cold, and egg prices skyrocket, which is a good opportunity for China to engage in this trade. Furthermore, canned frozen eggs are now widely sold in various parts of Europe, and exports are booming, and they are being sold at good prices. Moreover, the methods of breeding and manufacturing are being improved practically, and the future development is immeasurable. Other products such as pig bristles, oils, coarse cloth, hardware, minerals, monosodium glutamate powder, etc. produced in China have all increased in value in recent years, and it may not be difficult to develop them further in the British market in the future. This is the general situation of goods transported from China to Britain. To sum up, it is sufficient to prove that Sino-British trade has been booming in recent years. This is because my country is vast and rich in resources, with a large population, rich agricultural products, and strong purchasing power. At this time, the country is unified, the politics are reformed, and all construction is in full swing. The need for raw materials and industrial products is greater than in any other country. After local stability, the increase in exports of agricultural products can also be asserted. In terms of material matters, I deeply hope that friendly countries will provide kind assistance and cooperate sincerely, so that the spirit of human mutual assistance can achieve international mutual benefit. There is no prejudice in accepting or rejecting, and there must be a connection between what is and what is not. No matter which country in the world, if it can open up its vision, abide by fair trade, treat each other equally, and interact with us Chinese with the purpose of mutual assistance, a friendly attitude, sincere feelings, then our government and people will unite as one, based on the spirit of a civilized country with 5,000 years of history, the belief in reciprocity, and express our sincere sympathy and recognize it as a country of mutual benefit and assistance, so that we can work together to achieve co-existence and co-prosperity. If we violate this principle of fairness and friendship and hold on to our narrow minds, wrong ideas, and short-sightedness, and focus on developing our one-sided interests and satisfying our unilateral desires, and do not pay attention to our country's national conditions, public opinion, productivity, and purchasing power, the result will be a pity for trade between the two countries. Such regrets will be an obstacle to the development of trade between both parties. If we do not foresee and understand this, and transform it into nothingness, then even the shortest period of prosperity in international commercial history will inevitably decline and be eliminated by natural selection. I and all of you present here have the responsibility to eliminate this kind of regret and eliminate this kind of obstacle. I deeply hope that your government will be able to exert all efforts to eliminate all policies that hinder the commercial development of our two countries and all kinds of unequal facts, so as to enhance the goodwill of the people of our two countries, so that we can mutually assist and support each other to achieve the benefits of trade. The benefits of trade lie in mutual benefit, and the foundation of mutual benefit is built on equality, mutual assistance, friendship, and sincere feelings. I also hope that you will understand this meaning and be able to earnestly suggest to your government after your tour to the East to promote its realization and open up a bright and brilliant new record in the history of Sino-British trade, so that you will not have made this trip in vain, which is also my earnest hope.

Telegraphic Request to Stipulate the Number of Overseas Chinese Representatives in the National Assembly

Excellent Telegram from the Overseas Chinese Federation

The Overseas Chinese Federation, in view of the decision of the Fourth Plenary Session to convene the National Assembly on May 1st next year, telegraphed the central party and government organs yesterday, requesting that the number of overseas Chinese representatives be stipulated. The telegram is transcribed as follows: "Nanjing Central Party Headquarters, National Government, Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, Examination Yuan, Judicial Yuan, Control Yuan, Central Overseas Chinese Affairs Committee, Ministry of Interior, Ministry of Industry, all are aware that the Premier said, 'Overseas Chinese are the mother of the revolution.' The contributions of overseas Chinese to the country have been universally recognized. During the Wuchang Uprising, when the Premier returned to the East, overseas Chinese sages followed him to Shanghai to plan the revolution. The contributions of overseas Chinese were the reason for the proposal of overseas Chinese participation in politics. Finally, with the Premier's leadership, the upper levels belonged to the association and various overseas Chinese groups jointly requested at the lower levels and won six seats for overseas Chinese senators. Thus, even Yuan Shikai, who harbored hostility towards the political status of overseas Chinese, had to reluctantly acknowledge it. Since then, no warlord or bureaucrat dared to oppose overseas Chinese participation in politics. In 1925, the Northern Government nominally responded to the Premier's advocacy and convened the so-called National Representative Assembly, which also stipulated the number of overseas Chinese representatives as 16, divided into three representatives each from the British and Dutch colonies in Southeast Asia, and one representative each from Siam, Annam, Burma, Taiwan, the Philippines, and Russia, and a total of four representatives from Europe, America, Africa, Australia, Japan, and Korea. The National Assembly advocated by our Premier intends to have nine kinds of organizations, including modern industrial groups, chambers of commerce, educational associations, universities, provincial student federations, labor unions, agricultural associations, and joint opposition to Cao Kun and Wu Peifu's armies and political parties, each elect representatives to participate in the organization. Except for the eighth item, which has already passed, there is no need to discuss it. The industrial groups, chambers of commerce, labor unions, agricultural associations, educational associations, and universities referred to do not limit them to the domestic side. All overseas Chinese chambers of commerce, agricultural associations, labor unions, educational associations, universities, and other industrial groups that have been registered with the competent authorities before today should also be included in the participation. Based on the close relationship between the Premier and the overseas Chinese during his 40 years of revolutionary efforts, it can be asserted that the various organizations designated by the Premier must include overseas Chinese. Your Ministry is following the will and scheduling the National Assembly and is drafting the organizational law. We urgently telegraph this humble opinion, requesting that Your Ministry grant us the Overseas Chinese Federation.

Municipal Public Security Bureau Does Not Change Police Authority on Extra-Settlement Roads

Instructions from Bureau Chief Yuan

The Municipal Public Security Bureau instructed the district chiefs: "In order to enforce the order, it has been found that various Chinese and foreign newspapers today have a news item on the 'Police Authority Issue on Roads Built in the Extra-Settlement Area.' The article stated that starting from Monday, the Public Concession Police Station will be adding automobile patrol teams to patrol the roads built by the bureau outside the Concession. The head of the police station, Gan Laide, stated that the previous practice of Chinese police guarding the roads and stopping cars has also been stopped. Foreigners have not said anything about this, and he also stated that the issue of police authority on the roads of the bureau is being negotiated between the Municipal Council and the Chinese authorities. Although no date has been set for the discussion, it is expected to be soon. This bureau is responsible for protecting all Chinese and foreign people in the city. As winter prevention is approaching, it is especially our duty to conduct checks on pedestrians and vehicles in order to prevent all kinds of harmful events. The police authority on the roads built by the Public Concession Police Station outside the Concession was never entitled to be exercised by the Public Concession Police Station. The original police posts and inspection stations for checking pedestrians and vehicles set up by this bureau on each of these roads have not been stopped or changed. The aforementioned situation is extremely shocking. In addition to issuing orders and questioning the Superintendent of the Public Concession Police, please respond. The chiefs are hereby ordered to comply and continue to handle matters seriously as before. Please thoroughly investigate and report on whether the Public Concession Police has increased the number of automobile patrol teams on the roads in question and report back to us for verification. This order is hereby issued on December 9, 1920 of the Republic of China. Director Yuan Liang."

Beginning on January 1, 1931

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has received instructions from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce No. 14274 stating that the Trademark Law has been formulated and promulgated. It is now determined that the effective date of the Trademark Law will be January 1, 1931. After receiving the order, the bureau has instructed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to inform all industries.

Local News, Part Two

Dr. Wu Liande's Banquet for the Shipping Industry Last Night

Dr. Wu Liande, Director of the National Maritime Quarantine Service, hosted a banquet last night at 8 PM at the Old Carlton Hotel on Ningbo Road to foster camaraderie with leaders of the local shipping industry. Attendees included representatives from the Jianghai Customs, China Merchants, Taikoo, Jardine Matheson, Changxing, Lick茂, Ting Bao, Dalae, Pacific, French, 賚賜, 保和, Prince, Meishun, Tianxiang, Fulai, Nippon Yusen, Nissin, Osaka Shosen, and Java, among other Chinese and foreign shipping companies. In his address, Dr. Wu stated that since his appointment as Director of the Quarantine Service by the central government in July, he had intended to meet with leaders of the Shanghai shipping industry. Unfortunately, the sudden outbreak of the plague in the autumn kept him extremely busy until now. Maritime quarantine affairs had previously been managed concurrently by the Customs. After the Ministry of Health organized the National Quarantine Service, he took over the responsibility. He expressed his gratitude to the Customs authorities for their support whenever necessary. He acknowledged that all those present were giants in the shipping industry, deeply aware of the close relationship between maritime health and commerce, and therefore, there was no need for him to elaborate. The staff of his service were carefully selected for their knowledge and extensive experience, ensuring minimal conflict with the shipping industry during the execution of their duties. While there might occasionally be slight differences of opinion, once understanding was reached, disputes would immediately dissipate. The Health Service had promulgated the Maritime Quarantine Regulations in July, which were drafted with the assistance of Dr. Barker, Director of Quarantine for Australia and Director of the Plague Section of the Health Organization of the League of Nations. The regulations were carefully reviewed to ensure they were suitable for China, especially the port of Shanghai. Many experts considered them to be the most innovative quarantine regulations in the world. China had already ratified the 1926 Paris Health Convention, and his service would certainly comply with all the provisions of the convention and provide all necessary emergency quarantine measures. He hoped that all parties would cooperate sincerely to prevent the import and export of infectious diseases, benefiting everyone. He emphasized that the matter was difficult and requested everyone's friendly understanding and cooperation, so that they could mutually benefit from it. His service would treat ships and personnel from all countries equally, without any bias. Mr. Fan Den, representing Taikoo Shipping Company, then delivered a speech on behalf of the attendees from the shipping industry, after which the gathering dispersed.

Fu A-quan, Principal Offender in the Four Banks Robbery Case, Executed by Firing Squad

Composed a Poem Before Execution to Express his Aspirations

Also Claimed to be a Catholic

Seeking Confession to Ascend to Heaven

Smiled While Smoking a Cigarette Before Execution

Fu A-quan was among the criminals arrested by the police for intercepting and robbing funds prepared for delivery from the Four Banks warehouse. He was tried and convicted by the Special District Court. He was sentenced to death and his sentence was submitted to the higher authorities for approval. Upon receiving the order from above, the court notified the police to escort Fu A-quan from the Western Prison to the court yesterday afternoon. Judge Cheng Shangfeng opened the court to announce the verdict. The convict then expressed his grievances and said that since he was going to die, he had to compose a poem to express his aspirations. He also requested wine and food. Judge Cheng then provided him with paper and a pen. Fu wrote several lines that were neither a seven-character quatrain nor a five-character ancient poem, nor did they resemble modern poetry. The characters were also illegible and smudged. He was still trying to find joy in the face of death, and he was very pleased with himself. After reciting it, Judge Cheng ordered his handwriting to be attached to the file. Then, the bailiffs purchased food for Fu, who ate his fill. He then ordered the detectives to escort him to the Second Prison execution ground in Puhejing by car. The Special District Court Procuratorate dispatched Prosecutor Li, along with Police Chief Yang Deshan, Police Inspector Chen Xihui, Execution Officers Xue Bingzhang, Gu Hanqing, Zhu Wanyuan, and Zhang Chunsen, among others, to the execution ground by car. After the judge and Warden Dong took their seats, the convict was brought to the case. He stated that he was 22 years old, from Wuxian, and had worked as a calligrapher at the Hainal Bank on the Six Horse Road. He lived at the Yao Shuntai Rental Shop on Dagu Road and had a mother and a sister. His mother's surname was Zheng. He then requested a pen to write a will. At that time, Lu Bohong also performed a confession for him. The convict knelt on the ground and said, "I am a Catholic, please perform a confession for me so that I can ascend to heaven." Lu then sprinkled him with holy water. The convict then requested a cigarette, smoked it, and went to his execution smiling. The prosecutor then ordered the execution to be carried out. Police Chief Yang directed the execution officers to take him down and execute him by firing squad. The body was collected by the court for burial.

Issue of Releasing a Criminal for Attempted Murder

Two Judgments from the Former Mixed Court

Having Served Five and a Half Years

His Wife Applies for Release on his Behalf

Police Lawyer Raises an Objection

On June 14th of the fourteenth year of the Republic, the former Mixed Court sentenced Fang Ren to five years' imprisonment for attempted murder. When the case was reviewed with the assessor at the end of the term, the assessor consul sentenced him to ten years' imprisonment. He has now served five and a half years. A woman named Zheng Cai, claiming to be Fang Ren's wife, hired a lawyer to submit a petition to the Special District Court, stating that her husband had been sentenced to five years by Chinese officials and that his term had now expired, requesting that he be released on bail. After receiving the petition, the Special District Court notified the police. Police lawyer Ru Baoyi also submitted a petition, stating that the Municipal Council absolutely recognized the validity of the Mixed Court assessor consul's judgment and that there was no need to change it according to the recovery agreement, requesting that the woman's request be rejected. The petition consisted of thousands of words, which are not detailed here. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Wu opened the court. Lawyer Ru raised two preliminary questions: (1) Does this case fall under the jurisdiction of the Special District Court? (2) The surname of the convict and the surname of the petitioner do not have a single character in common. Is the petitioner actually his wife? Please make a ruling. Judge Wu then questioned Fang Ren about the reasons for requesting release. According to his statement, he was weak and suffering from tuberculosis, and the ten-year sentence had already been served for more than half the time. The court ordered Fang Ren to be taken back into custody for further review.

Russian Woman Creates Waves of Jealousy

Shoots and Wounds her Lover with a Gun

Sentenced to Two Years' Imprisonment with Probation

An Italian man, Bai Danla (transliteration), previously developed a relationship with a young Russian woman, Wufunuo, 26 years old, in Harbin, in northern China. Their friendship progressed into love, and they lived together like a married couple. Last year, they fled to Shanghai and resided at 228 Huanlong Road in the French Concession. Bai Danla worked at the Keda Photo Studio. Unexpectedly, Bai recently became involved with another Russian woman. One day, when Bai returned to his residence and took off his clothes, Wufunuo found a photo of Bai Danla and the Russian woman together in Bai's pocket. Jealousy flared up, and she started arguing with Bai. Bai took this opportunity to separate from Wufunuo and live elsewhere. Seven months have passed since then. Although Bai often visited Wufunuo, he only chatted and showed no affection. On the 28th of last month, Wufunuo called Bai Danla to her residence to talk. Wufunuo asked Bai if his relationship with the newly acquainted Russian woman was permanent. Bai replied that he had the freedom to marry her and that she should not interfere. Hearing this, Wufunuo was filled with anger and immediately returned to the bedroom. She took out a pistol and fired two shots at Bai, hitting his left arm. She was about to fire a third shot when the bullet jammed. At that time, Bai stepped forward and snatched the pistol. The police arrived and arrested Wufunuo. Bai went to the hospital for treatment. Yesterday, after his injuries healed, the police brought both parties to the French Concession Court for questioning. First, the police chief explained the situation. Then, Zhe Danla, a businessman, claimed that he had been living with the defendant, Wufunuo, for six years and that they had always been on good terms. However, the defendant was prone to nervous breakdowns. That day, her old illness recurred, and she attacked him with a gun. He requested a severe punishment. Wufunuo confessed that she had been living with the plaintiff for many years and that they had always been on good terms. Recently, he had found a new love and abandoned her like a worn-out shoe. That day, she was so angry that she intended to kill him and then commit suicide. Unexpectedly, the bullet jammed, and no one died. After confessing, she cried loudly. The Chinese and Western judges ruled that Wufunuo should not have attacked him with a gun. She was sentenced to two years' imprisonment with a five-year probation. The pistol was confiscated.

Deng Zhonghe's Experience with Extortion by Bandits

First Newspaper Advertisement, Then Sticky Notes

Finally, a Meeting Scheduled at Zhenhua Hotel for Payment

Detectives Ambushed in the Adjacent Room

The Bandits were Captured in One Fell Swoop Upon Entering the Room

Deng Zhonghe, the owner of the Daqing Cotton Cloth Store at 378 Ningbo Road, had previously been kidnapped. The police arrested several kidnappers, who were sentenced accordingly. Not long after the case was closed, Deng received another threatening letter from bandits stating that many of their comrades had lost their lives because of him, causing them great losses. They demanded a loan of 2,000 yuan to compensate the dead. If he was sincere, he could notify them by placing an advertisement in the newspaper. Deng followed the instructions in the letter and placed an advertisement in the newspaper. The next day, he received another letter from the bandits with a sticky note saying that they had seen the advertisement. Please stick this sticky note on the door and there would be movement. Deng did as he was told. On the 7th of this month, the bandits sent a letter scheduling Deng to go to the Zhenhua Hotel on Fuzhou Road at 4 pm on the 8th to discuss matters in a private room. They also instructed him to write "Sun Fengji" on the guest list and put the money, which must be in 100 yuan notes, in an envelope wrapped in newspaper, and place the package in the drawer of the table in the room he had booked. Someone would come to take it. On the morning of the 8th, Deng reported to the Old Zha police station, which sent detectives Liang Chengyu and Bao Tan Li Hanzhang to the Zhenhua Hotel to book two rooms, one being room 102. They put the package in this room and wrote "Sun Fengji, resident of room 102" on the guest card. The other room, room 105, was for the detectives to lie in ambush. At 11:30 pm, Zhang A-san from Zhenjiang entered room 102, claiming to be visiting Sun. He opened the drawer, took the package, and was about to leave when the detectives in the next room rushed out and arrested him on the spot. Yesterday, he was sent to the Special District Court. Police lawyer Ru Baoyi stated the details and requested a postponement to investigate accomplices. Judge Xu ordered the defendant to be detained for further questioning at a later date.

Young Mrs. Gu Sues her Husband for Separation

Another Woman on the Bed

The Father-in-Law is Deaf and Does Not Restrain Them

Enraged, She Sues for Separation

The Judge Tries to Mediate, but Fails

Gu Shoubai from Nanxun, residing at 40 Fanshi Lane, Mu'er Ming Road, has a son named Songgang, who is 25 years old. In the eleventh year of the Republic, his father arranged for him to marry Zhu Lianyun from Suzhou. Zhu is three years older than Songgang. They have been married for nine years and have four children, all lively and adorable, except for one who died young. Recently, Zhu has complained that her husband's behavior is improper and that he is extravagant. The millions of valuables she brought as a dowry have been almost entirely spent, and he still shows no remorse. At 11:30 am on the 30th day of the eighth month of the lunar calendar, Zhu returned home from outside and entered the bedroom. She suddenly saw a young woman on the bed, kissing Songgang. She was extremely angry but remained silent. Her husband, on the other hand, rebuked Zhu for disturbing their good dream. The father-in-law, Shoubai, pretended to be deaf and allowed his son to behave improperly without any family discipline. Zhu then took her eight-year-old eldest daughter, Wenwei, and moved to her mother's house at 41 Qingyuli, Xin Chongqing Road. She hired a lawyer to sue Gu Songgang in the Special District Court, requesting a decree of separation from Gu Songgang and that his father, Gu Shoubai, jointly bear the responsibility for alimony, paying 200 yuan per month for living expenses, depositing 30,000 yuan in cash in the bank as collateral, and compensating for the cost of pearls, gold, diamonds, and jewelry, amounting to 30,000 yuan, and that she be allowed to raise her eldest daughter, Wenwei. The Gu father and son were sued and hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to argue that the plaintiff had left on the 24th day of the sixth month of the lunar calendar under the pretext of returning to her home province to visit her sick mother and had not returned since. As the head of the family, Shoubai should provide for food and clothing. The plaintiff was instigated by others and demanded a separation for no reason. Shoubai had no legal obligation to support her, so there was no abandonment, etc. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenrong summoned the Songgang couple to court to confront each other. After hearing their respective statements, the court tried to mediate a reconciliation, but it was ineffective. The lawyers of both parties then began to debate. Finally, Judge Xu ordered that the judgment be postponed until the 13th.

Results of the Rotary Club's Grand Dance

Large Sums of Money Raised

Thanks to All Sectors

The Rotary Club of this city previously held a grand dance at the Dahua Hotel on October 24th and issued lottery tickets to raise funds for the Russian Children's Charity School. The results of the event, as reported previously, are now known. After deducting expenses totaling 730 yuan, the net profit was 16,200 yuan. Of this, 360 yuan has not yet been received, and the actual amount received is 15,840 yuan. The money has been deposited in the bank and is jointly managed by Zhu Boquan, K. Fukushima, E. F. Harris, F. E. Marden, and A. duPacdeMarsoulies. It is said that the donations from friends and colleagues are sufficient to cover all printing, publicity, and decoration costs, and all public donations can be used as a fund for the charity school. They are grateful and relieved. They are also deeply grateful to the ladies for their enthusiastic participation in the dance, the merchants for their eagerness to place advertisements, and all sectors for their enthusiastic donations to the prizes.

Recent News on the Demolition of Houses in Qingyun Lane

External Municipal Government's Approval

Since the incident of White Russians demolishing houses and injuring people in Qingyun Lane on September 10th, Xu Xinliu and other five Chinese directors of the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Concession took on the role of mediators. However, due to the ineffectiveness of the mediation, both parties resorted to litigation in court to seek a legal resolution. Therefore, the five Chinese directors stated that they would decline the responsibility of mediation because the case was under litigation. Since this dispute has been brought to the law, in principle, neither party should take any action until the legal process is over. It is heard that last month, the landlord, New Sassoon, sent a letter to mediator Xu Xinliu, stating that in order to implement the Municipal Council's plan to widen Tiantong Road and with the consideration of the Public Works Department, the land close to the road must be ceded to the Municipal Council in the near future. Therefore, in these few days, the company would definitely take "any necessary steps to prepare for the proceedings." Mr. Xu forwarded the letter to the Qingyun Lane Housing Association. Upon hearing the news, all the tenants of Qingyun Lane were alarmed, fearing that the foreign company would once again use the pretext of the Municipal Council's widening of the Tiantong Road surface to carry out a second violent demolition (because the south side of Qingyun Lane is directly on Tiantong Road). Therefore, they submitted a petition to the National Government's Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Wang, and the Shanghai Municipal Government's Mayor Zhang, and sent a letter to the Municipal Council's Director General Edward, requesting protection and a firm stop to the landlord's repeated illegal oppression, awaiting the court's resolution. Now, the replies from Foreign Minister Wang of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and Mayor Zhang of the Shanghai Municipal Government to the Qingyun Lane tenants have been obtained. Excerpts from the approval orders are as follows: Ministry of Foreign Affairs Storage Letter No. 22 Approval (All submitted documents have been examined. This case has previously been approved by the Ministry, which has sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Government stating that it has successively sent letters to the Public Concession Municipal Council and the Special District Court to handle the matter according to the law, etc. You should be informed accordingly.) Shanghai Municipal Government No. 1075 Approval (The submission has been examined. Since this case has been accepted by the court, all parties must be bound by it. The tenants of the lane should wait for the court's resolution. This approval).

French Concession Prohibits Reactionary Small Newspapers

The French police authorities have recently discovered that small newspapers such as "Kuaidao Daily", "Hard News", "Asahi News", "Warrior Daily", "Daily News", "Xuguang Daily", "Spring and Autumn Warrior", "Qianxie", and "Gangtie" often contain reactionary articles, which are deemed to be detrimental to public security. They have been banned from being sold in the concession. Yesterday, the political department and all plainclothes detectives were instructed to pay attention.

Yancheng County Magistrate Comes to Shanghai to Raise Disaster Relief Funds

Since Yancheng suffered from the ravages of bandit Yu Rentu, the people in the four villages have no food or clothing and are displaced. County Magistrate Cun Wei was saddened by the tragic situation. He came to Shanghai the day before yesterday with local gentry Ma Weili, Party Committee Hu Handong, and others to raise disaster relief funds. The Yancheng Students' Save the Homeland Association of this city, admiring his enthusiasm, has decided to hold a meeting at Qingliang Temple on the tenth of the month to welcome him and exchange opinions on various post-disaster relief matters.

Page 16

Regulations Affect Debt Raising

City Chamber of Commerce's Letter to the Ministry of Finance's Debt Raising Committee

The City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Bond Solicitation Committee of the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "We acknowledge receipt of your letter instructing us to promote the sale of the 19th year Short-Term Post-War Treasury Bonds. We have recorded the letter and notified all affiliated trade associations to comply. We have now received a letter from the Intestine Industry Association stating that they received your letter from the Bond Solicitation Committee of the Ministry of Finance urging them to solicit 2,000 yuan of bonds and instructing them to pay the amount as scheduled. Upon receiving this, we dispatched personnel to solicit donations from various trades, but despite our efforts, the results were nil, and we are deeply ashamed. When we approached trades that were not members of the association to solicit donations, we were met with stern refusals, claiming that since they were not members, they would not bother to solicit. The solicitors had no choice but to turn away. If we earnestly persuaded trades that were members of the association to donate, the members would argue that the association's regulations, submitted to the supervising authorities for approval, require that all trades, whether members or not, must comply with the regulations. Since the Ministry of Industry and Commerce rejected the case, newspapers have spread rumors that such bad practices have no legal or mandatory force, and that they violate good customs. The long-standing customs of the trade have been completely negated by the Ministry's rejection, destroying the historical and time-honored principles. This has caused many unscrupulous merchants to take the opportunity to disrupt market prices and monopolize the market, leading to repeated disputes. The association has no way to resolve these issues, and the members suffer losses and cannot maintain their business or secure their livelihoods. How can they have the surplus to subscribe to bonds? The trade association only places excessive obligations on its members. What is the value of this association? They claimed that they had reported the facts to the affiliated associations for review and that the members' claims were true. However, the bonds are also used for post-war reconstruction, which is very important. Therefore, under the circumstances, it is difficult to proceed. We have no choice but to express our difficulties and ask you to look into the matter and forward the letter to the Bond Solicitation Committee of the Ministry of Finance so that they may understand the situation. We beg you to consider and implement this matter."

Treatment of Female Silk Factory Workers

Social Affairs Bureau Summons Both Parties and Mediation is Successful

Regarding the issue of salary increases for female workers in this city, the Social Affairs Bureau summoned representatives from both labor and management the other day and scheduled a formal mediation for yesterday afternoon. The management representatives present were Shen Huachen, Xu Yunjian, and Zhang Peishen (represented by Ling Xiao), and the labor representatives were Song Xiaorong, Lu Cuizhen, Wu Suzhen, and nine others. Regarding the issue of salary increases, it was originally decided during the questioning the other day that the female workers would cancel the holiday bonus and the application for salary increases would remain the same as before, with four increments. However, the other day (the 7th), the silk factory association convened a meeting, and the representatives of the factories collectively stated that the silk market was depressed and that those who were still operating were already struggling. They could not meet the demands of the female workers. Therefore, the three representatives who attended yesterday stated that they could not comply. However, the female workers argued that during the previous talks, they had already decided to make concessions and cancel the holiday bonus. The monthly salary increase application would remain the same as before, with four increments. The management suddenly refused to comply, and the representatives could not return to the union to report. Therefore, they persisted for a long time. In the end, Wang Bingcai of the Social Affairs Bureau adopted a compromise solution and decided to change the application for salary increases from four increments to two increments. The female workers, realizing the factory's difficulties, had no choice but to agree. The management representatives also respected the mediator's wishes and complied. A formal agreement was then signed and drafted as follows: (1) The wages of female workers in all silk factories in the city shall be temporarily calculated at 85% of the original amount. (2) The holiday bonus shall be temporarily canceled. (3) The salary increase (i.e., monthly bonus) to which female workers are entitled each month shall be temporarily given two increments (one increment for ten days, two increments for sixteen days. However, the labor party shall not cite this point as a precedent when wages are restored to their original state in the future). (4) When the factory's business improves, the labor party may request the restoration of the original wages, but the period for which wages are reduced shall be delayed until the end of May of the twentieth year. (5) The treatment of workers in double-shift factories is different from that of workers in single-shift factories. If there are any increases or decreases, they must be submitted to the government for approval separately. (6) This agreement shall take effect from November (New Sound News Agency).

Change to National Calendar for Termination Dates

Labor Contracts Stipulating Lunar Calendar Dates Should be Changed to National Calendar Dates

The City Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Pen and Ink Trade Association yesterday, stating: "We acknowledge receipt of your letter stating that you have reviewed the case of Ermiaotang Yiji's termination of Hu Hansheng and others and requesting a change in interpretation to use the national calendar for handling. We have reported the matter to the Social Affairs Bureau for review. We have now received approval No. 442, which states that we have examined the approval statement. The bureau's instruction No. 2962 is in accordance with the Municipal Government's Bulletin No. 107, which states that after the expiration date of previous lunar calendar contracts, the date shall be calculated according to the national calendar, which is deferred by one month, which is a simple and easy method. This interpretation covers all civil contracts and is not limited to debt payments. If the labor and management conditions in this case are indeed difficult to implement in practice, both parties may amend them according to the national calendar. We hereby reply to your letter for your information and notification."

Yesterday, the Chinese Industrial Association and the Chinese General Federation of Industry and Commerce telegraphed the National Government, saying to Chairman Chiang of the National Government: We humbly observe that since the completion of the unification of our National Government, political construction has been carried out in an orderly manner, and the main points of various policies have also been formulated. We humbly note that the current Minister of Industry, Kong Xiangxi, was initially promoted to the position of Minister of Industry in Guangdong due to his revolutionary achievements. Later, after the capital was moved south, he followed the Chairman in presiding over industry and commerce, dedicating his efforts to construction and safeguarding industrial administration. Hong Sheng and others have personally witnessed this and there is no need for further elaboration. Recalling when Minister Kong initially assumed the position of Minister of Industry, it was during the 17th year of the Republic of China. At that time, the overall situation in the Southeast was just stabilizing and the Northern Expedition had not yet succeeded. The Hubei rebellion was unprecedented in decades. Minister Kong shouldered heavy responsibilities and was able to handle them with ease. In less than three years in office, important industrial and commercial facilities such as commodity inspection have been established in order. Labor-capital cooperation has been established as a plan. National measurement has been planned for unification. Scientific school management has been engaged in promotion. Industrial and commercial visits have been set up as a bureau to handle them specially. All other development affairs related to industry can be practically implemented in an orderly manner. The interests of the party and the country are known to be done without fail, and the benefits of industrial administration are seen without fail to be raised. His transcendent thinking and sincere handling of affairs are truly outstanding talents of today. Yesterday, we received news from the capital that Minister Kong has submitted his resignation, deeply alarming us. We humbly believe that Minister Kong's integrity is incorruptible and his reasoning is detailed and clear. Therefore, although his tenure as minister has not been long, his achievements have been remarkable. At this time of national and social turmoil, when the suffering of the national industry has not yet been resolved, even if Minister Kong himself seeks to retire, the various industries in the national industrial sector cannot sit idly by and watch him retreat into seclusion, causing the progress of the entire plan to stagnate. It would be fortunate for the party and the country, and fortunate for the industry. Abolition of Exorbitant Taxes on Sichuan Silk to be Implemented

Reply from the Ministry of Finance to the National Federation of Commerce

Yesterday, the National Federation of Commerce received a reply from the Ministry of Finance, No. 11491, stating: "We have received your submission. Upon investigation, the various military forces in Sichuan Province collect miscellaneous taxes on silk cocoons in their respective defense zones. The cost of each box of silk is only about 600 yuan, but the tax is as high as 120-130 yuan, resulting in excessive costs and complete losses. If no measures are taken to seek relief urgently, Sichuan silk will decline day by day, which is crucial to the livelihood and security of the people of Sichuan Province. Before the implementation of the abolition of levies in the province, all exorbitant taxes and miscellaneous taxes in the defense zones of the province should be appropriately reduced or exempted in order to save it. This Ministry has telegraphed the Commander-in-Chief of the Army and Navy to promptly instruct the commanders of the 21st, 28th, and 29th Armies of Sichuan Province to comply and implement, and to abolish the newly established Jiangfang Import Tax in Chongqing first, in order to alleviate the hardships of merchants. You are hereby informed. This is the order."

Yu Shun and Jiang Xin Vessels Run Aground

It is common for ships to have accidents due to shallow water on the upper reaches of the Yangtze River. The Yu Shun vessel of the China Merchants Bureau was transporting goods to Wuhan this time. When it arrived at Hankou, the river water was receding greatly. The vessel was anchored in the heart of the river, but the passengers demanded that the vessel move to the dock for the sake of picking up goods. The shipowner initially refused, but the passengers said that the riverbank had 25 feet of draft and could be moved. Unexpectedly, the Yu Shun vessel ran aground during the process of moving. At that time, there was no towing vessel in Hankou, so the Yu Shun was stranded for a day and night until yesterday when the Lijian vessel from Changsha arrived in Hankou and sent it to rescue. The goods in the vessel are being unloaded. It is expected that the vessel can be rescued today. Also, the Jiang Xin vessel transported soldiers from Beijing to Yangluo this time to suppress bandits. After the soldiers landed in Yangluo, the Jiang Xin set off for Hankou. When it entered the Yangtze River in Hankou, it was also at low tide. The vessel ran aground on the shoal because the vessel was still loaded with a lot of cargo and had not been unloaded, so it was difficult to tow. Yesterday, it was reported that the cargo was being lightered first to reduce the load, and then towed today. The hulls of the two vessels are generally not badly damaged, and the passengers are getting on and off safely.

Special News from the Yangtze River Shipping Industry

Hunan rice can be transported. This year, Hunan rice has a bumper harvest and the provincial government has lifted the ban on transporting it to other provinces. Afterwards, because the passport fee for Hunan rice leaving the province was 5 yuan per stone, the previous procurement was temporarily stopped for a long time. Now the Hunan authorities have agreed to relax the restrictions. Yesterday, the various wheel companies in this port received a telegram from Changsha saying that Hunan rice can be loaded and transported in large quantities to Shantou and Guangdong, and then transferred to Shanghai by boat. However, because the river water in Hunan is shallow and cannot be transported directly, shallow-water barges have been dispatched to load and transport Hunan rice leaving the province.

Cargo Accumulated in Nanxun due to Water Transport: Due to the Communist Party's disturbances in Jiangxi, cargo along the Nanxun Road has been suspended for a long time, and the accumulated cargo has been increasing day by day. This time, the Central Government sent troops to Jiangxi to suppress the Communists, and the area between Nanchang and Jiujiang has been cleared. Merchants are eager to transport the accumulated cargo to Shanghai. However, the Nanxun Road lacks vehicles and needs to be transported urgently. Therefore, Jiangxi merchants negotiated with Shanghai Sanbei China Merchants and other wheel companies and decided that from the 10th of this month, cargo from Nanchang and other areas will be transported by waterway to Nanxun. Special barge shifts will be added at Hukou to transport cargo to Shanghai. The Sanbei Company has complied with the requirements of the Jiangxi merchants and has telegraphed Xuan'an Yang'an and other vessels to start the Hukou Nanxun shift from today. China Merchants has also dispatched shifts to start sailing to Shanghai to transport Nanchang cargo, which has been restored today.

Henan Tobacco Leaves Arrived in Shanghai: 30,000 pieces of Henan Xuchang tobacco leaves transported to Shanghai, which were detained in Hankou, have been released after Yu Qiaqing and others telegraphed Hubei for consultation. The first batch of 5,000 pieces has been transported to Shanghai by the Sanbei China Merchants Bureau and unloaded in Shanghai yesterday.

Compensation for the Feihu Vessel Has Been Allocated

180,000 Yuan

The Feihu vessel of the Sanbei Company was rammed by a naval vessel in front of the China Merchants Bureau Wharf in Hankou on February 23 this year and sunk in the Yangtze River. Afterwards, the Sanbei Company sent technicians and workers to Hankou to salvage it for three months, but it could not be salvaged. The insurance company said that the accident of the vessel was outside the scope of ordinary beaches and claimed that it was not insured for military risks and refused to pay compensation after several negotiations. Until last month, because there was no hope of salvage, the rescue was abandoned. Yu Qiaqing, the owner of Sanbei, immediately submitted a request to the headquarters and the Navy Department to compensate for the loss of the vessel in order to maintain the capital. Yu entered Beijing several times to contact Chairman Chiang and the naval authorities, and now it has been completely resolved. The headquarters has recognized the loss of the Feihu vessel at 180,000 yuan, which has been received by Yu. It has been decided to build a new vessel to replace it.

Measures for Sunday Holidays with Pay for Daily Workers in Japanese Factories

Amendment by the Central Executive Committee

Notification by the Civil Training Committee

The Mass Training Committee of the Shanghai Special City Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang has issued a notice to the labor and capital representatives of various factories in the city regarding the announcement of matters and cases. The notice of the Central Executive Committee No. 17080 states that regarding the factory's annual shutdown dates and the measures for Sunday holidays with pay for daily workers, the 70th Standing Committee of the Central Executive Committee previously resolved that the factory's annual shutdown dates should be based on the revolutionary memorial days and memorial ceremonies, which are January 1, March 12, March 29, July 9, October 10, and November 12, and one more day for May 1 Labor Day, for a total of seven days. The measures for Sunday holidays with pay for daily workers (workers whose wages are calculated on a daily basis) "should be handled in accordance with the legally effective group agreements or work contracts. If there is no agreement, it should be determined according to whether the work is long-term or short-term." After the announcement of the above measures, various factories in various places have different situations in employing workers and the method of paying wages on weekdays, and there is no definite standard for long-term and short-term employment in fact, so it is difficult to handle. After inquiring about the opinions of the three departments of Industry, Commerce, Transportation, and Railway from the Central Training Department, the amendment was submitted to the Central Executive Committee for discussion at the 115th Standing Committee. It was agreed that since there is no definite standard for long-term and short-term employment in fact, it should not be used as the basis for whether to pay wages. Even if there is no formal contract between the factory and the workers, there should be some agreement on such issues at the time of employment. The original resolution on those without an agreement is not necessary, so it was resolved to amend the section on the measures for Sunday holidays with pay for daily workers in the original resolution of the 70th Standing Committee as follows: "...As for the measures for Sunday holidays with pay for daily workers (workers whose wages are calculated on a daily basis), it should be handled in accordance with the legally effective group agreements or work agreements." The amendment of the resolution should be notified to all party departments for their information and to be forwarded to their respective subordinates for their information. In addition to informing the Social Affairs Bureau by letter, all labor and capital parties in the city's factories must be informed.

The Procuratorate Scheduled to Burn Items

Recently, the amount of opium being transported into Shanghai has been increasing day by day. Some unscrupulous merchants disregard local security and often smuggle and leak opium, morphine, and red pills and other drugs in order to profit from them. They gather people to smoke or sell them, causing harm. The Shanghai Local Court Procuratorate has been vigorously enforcing the ban on opium and has been doing its best to handle it. Opium, morphine, and other drugs have been seized and routinely burned. It has now been decided to burn all the smoking paraphernalia seized from January to June of the 19th year at 2:00 p.m. on the 13th of this month in the open space next to the west side of the court. It is estimated that in the six months from January to June of the 19th year, there will be 5,301 taels and 5 qian of opium soil, 49 jin and 4 taels of opium dross, 112 jin of red pills, 31 taels and 6 qian of morphine, 8 jin and 6 taels of heroin, and 2,925 pieces of other smoking paraphernalia. It is also heard that letters were sent to various agencies yesterday inviting them to send representatives to the site to supervise the destruction of the tickets in order to show prudence.

Yang Guanshang Disappeared in Shanghai

Demanding 10,000 Yuan for Ransom

Yang Guanshang, a native of Wuxi, 49 years old, was formerly the manager of the Yikang Yarn Factory in the port. He has a wife, children, and meager assets. He is quite weak and enjoys socializing. Yang came to Shanghai at the end of last month to pay his respects at the funeral of the Xue family. He took a car and stayed at the Zhenhua Hotel on Fourth Ma Road in the Public Concession. Then, on the 3rd of this month, he went to congratulate his close friend surnamed Sun, and then suddenly disappeared. Because Yang did not return for many days and there was no news, his family immediately sent someone to Shanghai to look for him without success, so they were even more panic-stricken. Unexpectedly, at about 9:00 p.m. the night before last, when the person was searching around, he suddenly received a quick letter from Yang's home, stating that the family had received a letter requiring them to prepare 10,000 yuan to go to a certain port to negotiate. After receiving the letter, the person returned to Wuxi early yesterday morning.

The Huishi Police Station Continues to Capture Bandits

The Huishi Police Station previously arrested a bandit named Bi Yongcheng. Under interrogation, he confessed that his accomplices were hiding in the countryside west of Shanghai. Therefore, the detective Shang Wu led detectives to the village late at night on a certain day to arrest them. There were many dogs in the village, and they barked when they heard footsteps in the middle of the night. The bandits who were hiding heard the dogs barking and knew that strangers had arrived or that it was bad for them, so they fled in the dark. Although the detectives saw dark shadows, they were not familiar with the village roads and could not pursue them, so they were allowed to escape. The night before last, they went to arrest them again and successively captured Song Wenyi, Xue Luyu, Zai Wenfang, and Sun Xiaolun, all of whom were Jianghuai migrants. Yesterday, they were escorted to the Special District Local Court for interrogation by Judge Sun. They were ordered to be detained and tried together with Bi Yongcheng.

Later, Mr. Huang Weimin, the backbone of the newspaper, stopped publication for a few issues from the 207th issue for the sake of improving quality and hired writers. It is also heard that the newspaper welcomes subscriptions and the establishment of consignment locations in various ports. The address is 301 Tongan Lane, Hankou Road.

The Cigarette Exchange Trade Association held its 13th Executive Committee meeting yesterday. Over ten committee members attended. The chairman reported on the handling of various matters. (3) Recently, due to the daily decline in foreign prices, the market has been chaotic. The previously established price list for the trade should be revised. It was resolved that the secretariat should issue a notice to convene the Evaluation Committee on the 11th of this month to evaluate prices. (4) The Cigarette and Alcohol License Tax Collection Office has been collecting 8% of Customs Treasury Bills from the trades in the North and South Cities for a long time. The amount collected should be checked. It was resolved that personnel in charge in the North and South Cities should directly check the seals at their respective offices and report to the association for review. (5) The end of the National Calendar year is approaching soon, and the government has repeatedly issued clear orders to comply with its implementation. It was resolved that the association should earnestly notify all tradesmen to comply and include a summary explanation of the benefits and drawbacks in the price list to avoid continuing old habits. (6) The tradesmen in the South City proposed that it was reported that the Fourth Plenary Session of the Kuomintang had resolved to implement business tax reform on January 1, 1931, to reduce the burden on merchants and civilians. The deadline for this is approaching, and the trades have repeatedly suffered from similar business taxes, such as license fees and public sales fees, causing extreme pain. It was asked how to discuss requesting the authorities to abolish them. It was resolved that the tradesmen in the North City should first be consulted to prepare a detailed letter of justification before deciding on the course of action. The rest is omitted.

In addition to publishing a notice in the newspaper, we should also send a letter to you for review and transmission to the traders under your authority for information, so that preparations can be made in advance and earnestly implemented. Please do not hesitate to assist in the public cause."

To the Editor of the News Department of the Shen Bao Newspaper,

I was surprised to read the news item in your newspaper's "News" column on December 9, which reported on the rickshaw pullers in the Public Concession protesting the fare increase. Sincerely,
